# Task: Generate Search Variant Mapping from Anime Song Database

You are analyzing an anime song database to create an efficient search variant mapping for FTS5 full-text search.

## Context

I have a SQLite database containing anime song names. Users often search using:
- ASCII equivalents of special characters (e.g., searching "masterpiece" for "M@STERPIECE")
- Romanization variants (e.g., "ou" vs "ō", "uu" vs "ū")
- Leetspeak substitutions (e.g., "3" for "e", "0" for "o")
- Common Unicode variants (e.g., "×" for "x")

Currently, my search generates too many variants at query time, causing performance issues (13ms CPU, 1.5s wall time).

## Your Task

### Step 1: Analyze the provided song names

I will provide you with all unique song names from my database. Analyze them to identify:
1. Which special characters are actually used in song names
2. What their ASCII equivalents should be

### Step 2: Create a character mapping

Generate a JSON mapping of special characters to their ASCII base form:

```json
{
  "@": "a",
  "0": "o",
  "ō": "o",
  "ū": "u",
  "3": "e",
  "×": "x",
  "★": "",
  "♪": "",
  ...
}
```

Rules:
- Only include characters that ACTUALLY APPEAR in the song names
- Map to the most likely ASCII character a user would type
- For decorative symbols (★, ♪, ♡), map to empty string ""
- For punctuation variants (×, ‐, —), map to their ASCII equivalent

### Step 3: Create a normalized song name table

For songs with special characters, provide the normalized version:

```json
{
  "M@STERPIECE": "masterpiece",
  "Zettai zetsumei × Zettai zetsumei": "zettai zetsumei x zettai zetsumei",
  "Hōkago Tea Time": "houkago tea time",
  ...
}
```

### Step 4: Provide statistics

Report:
- Total songs analyzed
- Number of songs with special characters
- Top 20 most common special characters and their frequency
- Any characters you're unsure about

## Output Format

Provide your response as valid JSON:

```json
{
  "stats": {
    "totalSongs": 50000,
    "songsWithSpecialChars": 5000,
    "topSpecialChars": [
      {"char": "ō", "count": 1234, "mappedTo": "o"},
      {"char": "@", "count": 567, "mappedTo": "a"},
      ...
    ]
  },
  "charMapping": {
    "@": "a",
    "ō": "o",
    ...
  },
  "normalizedSongs": {
    "M@STERPIECE": "masterpiece",
    ...
  }
}
```

## Notes

- Focus on PRACTICAL mappings that users would actually search for
- Ignore case (we handle case-insensitivity separately)
- Japanese characters (hiragana, katakana, kanji) should be kept as-is, not mapped
- Only romanization helpers (ō→o, ū→u) should be included
